And it's stick straight. My hair is the type that typically makes hairdressers weep, curse, and force shampoo girls to run to the store for more bobby pins. It has very little body and resists all attempts to \\"stay\\" in updos, etc. (at least not without 75 bobby pins and a stiff lacquer of hair spray). And, when it stays down, it looks dull and limp and lifeless. All the things hair product marketing typically preys on. So, most mornings it goes back in a ponytail or up in one of those claw clips. About the only thing I HAVE done with my hair is slightly over-process it and damage it with repeated hair colorings in a desperate attempt to make it more interesting. That being said, I ordered this product as a last ditch attempt. I followed the directions another reviewer posted: Add five pumps to top and sides of head, five more pumps to middle-ish section, and five pumps to ends. NOTE: Again, I have shoulder length hair and based on other feedback its best to glob it on there (more is more), so use that as your guide. After applying, I cupped both hands under the shower water until about half-full, splashed over top of my head, and massaged conditioner in for a count of 60-75 seconds. After that, I used a shower comb (not the WEN variety, a cheaper CVS plastic version) to comb through working from top of head back and down (making sure to pay attention to right above the ears--one of the potentially dryer spots for me). After combing through a couple times, I used a plastic clip (The Crane Clip--also available on Amazon) to gently hold the hair up. I do the hair first (to allow the product to sit on my hair as long as possible--probably between 10 and 15 minutes) and then do the rest of my shower routine. After finishing up everything else, I unclip my hair and rinse. I tend to lean towards over-rinsing because I want to make sure I've gotten all the product out. I now LOVE my hair!!! The first day or two I had a little bit of difficulty with it feeling dry and with a little bit of static (not enough to be super distracting, more of just a hint). I adjusted the amount of the product I was using as a leave-in and that solved the problem. Either that or my hair just needed to adjust. My dull, limp, lifeless, ugh hair is now shiny, has a naturally full amount of body, feels soft and light and makes me literally want to do the shampoo commercial head toss! And it's not just me, I've gotten tons of comments (from my fiancee--who NEVER notices those kinds of things, to co-workers--who almost don't believe I didn't get some expensive salon treatment, to my sisters--who have similar hair types and will be receiving their first bottle for xmas). I haven't had ANY of the problems that previous reviewers have described. That being said, this review is based on just a week's worth of use. Additionally, I have hair that's both thin and fine (which the product seems to have the most success with). One of the aforementioned co-workers has a different hair type then mine and she's going to try the Fig variety. I've encouraged her to post a review on her experiences too. Unfortunately, it's freaking expensive. Several other reviewers have commented that the Sally's Beauty generic brand works just as well, so I may give that a try and will update my review based on that experience. If it doesn't work as well, I'm coming back to WEN. It's just works too darn well!

  171. I have to admit I saw this product one evening on an infomercial. It intrigued me, but like any infomercial I was skeptical so I read many many reviews to see how well a cleansing conditioner worked. I found mixed reviews. I hate buying straight from infomercial sites, because 9/10 times there is usually an automatic renewal shipping which I hate (and WEN does). So I was thrilled when I found this on Amazon, like everything else I can find on amazon. I am a die hard amazon fan and devoted customer. :) Now on to the actual product review. It took a little getting used to and I did see improved results after about a good month of use. Meaning it took that long to adjust to how much I should use, technique, etc. I was a die hard Burt's Bees shampoo / conditioner fan before I switched over. I have finer hair that never really could get enough moisture from conditioners. The ends would always feel dry, no matter how often I go for trims. My hair would also snag and tangle easily also, as well as being really really frizzy. This cleansing conditioner calmed my hair and really moisturized it. It doesn't feel heavy, doesn't look greasy, and I have no more fly away hairs. My routine. To give an idea of how much I use. This is according to the 32 oz tall bottle (I found one pump from the tall bottle is about equal to 2 pumps from the small bottle - if you are pumping slow). It is true, more is better. I have medium to fine hair that comes to the bottom of my bra strap in the middle of my back. I will wet down my hair thoroughly and apply 5-7 full slow pumps to the top of my head to start out. I will then apply 3-5 slow pumps to the sides of my head by my temples, concentrating by my ear (which tends to be a grease spot for me if I do not clean there well enough). I then apply about 10 slow pumps to the ends of the hair, working up to my scalp. I will then pile my hair on top of my head and message while adding 2-3 pumps to the pile and work to theback of my head and nape of my neck. I will then cup my hands to catch some water and splash it to the top of my head. It may sound a bit ridiculous, but it does really help with promoting the lather (it doesn't foam though). I then let my hair down and take a fine tooth comb and comb through my hair once to remove tangles and dead loose hair (starting at the ends and working my way up). I will then apply 2-3 more pumps, quickly message, and wind my hair up and clip it. I leave my hair soak while I wash my body, face, shave, etc. I then rinse my hair thoroughly. This is so important - rinsing thoroughly. The directions do recommend to give a 1-2 pump and message into the ends after showering as a leave in conditioner. I do not leave any in. I found that did make my hair look a bit greasy afterwords. I would probably do that before swimming though, haven't tried it yet though. Once I exit the shower with thoroughly rinsed hair. I will blot my hair dry with a towel, wet my hands, then apply two pumps of the WEN Sweet almond mint styling creme, concentrating at the ends and length of the hair. I stay away from my temples, but what ever is left on my hands I will then run through the top of my head. I do not blow dry my hair, I leave it dry naturally. I think the most important thing that helps eliminate my fly aways is I do not comb or brush my hair when it is wet anymore (except while showering with the cleansing conditioner in it). I just use my fingers until my hair is completely air dried, for my hair does not tangle anymore after using this cleansing conditioner. I have noticed my hair is slowly becoming more wavy with body and I am finding less and less hair left in the drain of the shower. I hope this reviewed helped and is a bit insightful.

  389. I started using wen in late 2012. For the first few months my hair improved but I have since noticed different affects that I should share. With wen, my hair felt and looked softer and shinier without being oily-shiny, seemed to retain moisture longer and feel cleaner longer than before, seemed to hold bounce longer and not feel as flat and weighted by the end of the day as before, and felt like it was becoming stronger or more flexible so as to not break under slight pressure. During the day it felt great running my fingers through my hair and feeling it smoothly slide back into place below my shoulders in a wispy fashion. Wen made my hair feel refreshed any hour of the day. I had been using pantene shampoo and conditioner regularly before and I decided to invest in trying wen because with pantene my mid-length, straight, naturally thin hair would become flat, oily and unbearably limp by afternoon on a daily basis. I had what I would describe as average (not above average) daily hair loss due to daily shampooing of mid-length hair. Before using wen, there would be some hairs caught on top of the shower drain which I would remove daily after a shower. For a time being after wen I believed I was losing less hair down the drain, although I could see hair strands being loosened by wen along with the detangling benefits of distributing wen throughout the hair. Because I was sold after several month's use--the transformation was wonderful and worth even the price--I told myself this was part of the transformation process and I focused on the detangling benefits and how great my hair felt and looked and I would have continued paying for wen. Then, maybe 6+ months later I noticed the shower drain started to clog to the point where water was trapped a couple of inches above floor level and the amount of draining time after showering steadily increased. The shower would drain so it was not an immediate plumbing concern but it would take longer to drain, not to mention that the water level got to the point where I could kick and swoosh water around my shower floor while I showered. When I finally got around to unscrewing the drain cover, I used one of those flexible pipe grabbers and pulled out what appeared to be a chunk of long hair meshed together in the ironic shape of a pony tail as if all that drained hair had somehow collected itself in a natural flowing bundle not quite able to be pushed out by water beyond the drain catch points yet--and it was definitely my hair. The amount of hair in that mesh looked about the same amount of hair left on my head if I was to pull my hair into a pony tail. I am not kidding. I was a little shocked, scared, and uncertain of what could have caused this. My shower drain has never clogged like this before. For a good moment I questioned whether wen contributed to this, but I really didn't want to believe because I really loved wen and what I felt it was doing for my hair but also because I didn't have a smoking gun and didn't want to jump to conclusions. One reason I told myself was that maybe wen didn't make my hair fall out more than any other shampoo but that maybe it just made the hairs flow pass the drain more and because of this, I wasn't able to pick up hair after each shower like before. So I continued using wen up until early 2014. I really was enchanted by how it made my hair feel and to this day I probably would have continued using wen except that in early 2014, although the clogged drain hasn't occurred again, I checked the drain pipe out of curiosity and happened to pull out a similar meshed hair pile that this time appeared to have about 1/3 equal of the amount of hair left on my head. I look back and wondered if my increasingly wispy hair feeling was due to the issue that my hair was becoming less full. Note I did not lose hair in patches, it was just thinning to the point where my pony tail was starting to look like a man's pony tail. For sometime during the later months of wen use I did feel my hair was looking sadly thinner (I had this feeling before becoming aware of any other reviewers' potential hair loss--I thought it was in my head). This observation coupled with recent searches for connections to possible hair loss has informed my personal decision to stop using wen. I am a real customer, not with any other motive than to share my experience. I can't say I know that wen contributed or was the sole or partial contributor or that you should not try wen yourself but what I do want to say is that if you experience hair loss, trust your gut instinct and beware of going down that denial road--the road that you want this miracle to continue working so badly. Look for alternatives or simply take a break from wen for a while. You can always go back to using wen with the click of an order button but you will take longer to regrow hair regardless of the primary source of hair loss. I decided I would rather have naturally thin flat oily bad hair days than thinning beautiful feeling hair days and this is certainly not a happy ending for me--not that wen is to blame but maybe I too just need a break. Best wishes.
